Dear Mr. Gaston:
In general accordance with the scope of services outlined in our fee proposal dated
October 9, 2015, we observed the grading and backfilling operations for the Kamalani
Increment 1 project. In general, our geotechnical engineering observations during the
grading and backfilling operations were performed from March 31, 2016 through
February 16, 2017. Our field observations and test results are provided in the attached
earthwork observation and testing report dated March 21, 2017.
| certify that Geolabs performed the earthwork compaction tests. To the best of our
knowledge, it is our professional opinion that the grading work observed by Geolabs has
been constructed in general conformance with the approved plans and Standard
Specifications for Public Works Construction, County of Maui, the geotechnical report, and
subsequent recommendations provided for the above project.
If you have questions or need additional information, please contact our office.
Respectfully submitted,

Earthwork Observation and Testing Report 
Kamalani Increment 1

TMK: 3-8-04:030 
Reference: Report by Hawaii Geotechnical Consulting, dated September 15, 2014 
entitled  "Geotechnical Investigation Report, 
Kihei Residential Subdivision,  
Kihei, Maui, Hawaii” 
Grading Permit No.: G2016/044 
Dear Mr. Gaston: 
This report summarizes our earthwork observation and testing services, performed 
during the grading and infrastructure installation work for the Kamalani Increment 1 project 
from March 31, 2016 through February 16, 2017. 
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS 
The Kamalani Increment 1 development (approximately 17.4 acres) is in the North 
Kihei area on the Island of Maui, Hawaii. The project site is bounded approximately by 
Waiakoa Gulch to the north, Kaiwahine Street and residential neighborhood to the south, 
the proposed Increment II to the east, and the Piilani Highway to the west. 
Based on the information provided, it is desired to develop the property into a 
residential housing providing approximately 170 multi-family units for development. We 
understand the overall Kamalani project will be constructed in two separate phases. The 
Increment 1 portion of the development will encompass about 13.25 acres over the 
western and central portions of the property. The Increment 2 portion of the development 
will encompass the remaining 4.15 acres of the development situated to the east of the 
property.  
A&B Properties, Inc. 
Page 2 
W.O. 7304-00 (Grading Permit No. G2016/044) 
March 21, 2017 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
The new buildings generally will consist of single-story structures. Some of the 
building areas will be developed into building pads. New spine road, side artery roads, 
driveways and underground utility lines will also be constructed at the project site.  The 
layout of the residential development is shown on the Site Plan, Plate 1. 
EARTHWORK OPERATIONS 
Rojac Construction Co., Ltd. performed the site grading operations, base pavement 
construction, and utility line installation. The asphalt placement was constructed by Maui 
Paving LLC. The site grading work consisted of subgrade preparation, placement and 
compaction of fills and backfills, pavement construction, and utility trench excavation and 
backfill. 
Following the clearing and grubbing operations, the excavated subgrades or areas 
designated to receive fills were scarified to a minimum depth of 8 inches, 
moisture-conditioned to near optimum moisture content, and compacted to a minimum of 
90 percent of the maximum dry density as determined in accordance with ASTM D1557 
(Modified Proctor).  The compaction requirement was increased to a minimum of 
95 percent relative compaction for finished subgrades subjected to vehicular traffic. 
During placement of the imported non-expansive select granular fill, the fill 
materials were generally placed in near-level lifts, brought to near optimum moisture 
content, and compacted to a minimum of 90 percent of the maximum dry density 
determined in accordance with ASTM D1557 (Modified Proctor). The base course under 
the AC pavement was generally placed in near-level lifts, brought to above the optimum 
moisture content, and compacted to a minimum of 95 percent of the maximum dry density 
determined in accordance with ASTM D1557 (Modified Proctor).   
New utility connections were installed to serve the new development. In general, a 
bedding layer consisting of 6 inches of sand was provided below the piping and manholes 
for uniform support. Tan coralline silty sands were also used for the trench backfill up to 
about 12 inches above the pipes to provide adequate support around the pipes and to 
reduce the compaction effort on the initial trench backfill. The trench backfill was placed in 
12-inch level loose lifts and mechanically compacted to no less than 90 percent relative 
compaction. Where trenches are below pavement areas, the upper 3 feet of the trench 
backfill below the pavement grade was compacted to a minimum of 95 percent relative 
compaction. 
During the site grading operations, samples of the on-site and imported materials 
utilized as fill and backfill materials were obtained and transported to our office for testing. 
The maximum dry densities and optimum moisture contents were established in our 
laboratory in general accordance with ASTM D1557 (Modified Proctor), and the test 
results are summarized on Plate 2. 
A&B Properties, Inc. 
Page 3 
W.O. 7304-00 (Grading Permit No. G2016/044) 
March 21, 2017 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
Field density tests were performed during the fill and backfill operations on an 
as-needed basis to confirm our field observations as variations in construction procedures 
and soil conditions were noted. A total of 2162 field density tests were performed using the 
nuclear probe method in accordance with ASTM D6938. Results of the compaction tests 
performed are summarized on Plates 3.1 through 3.141 of this report. These tests were 
performed on the prepared ground surfaces and on constructed fills and backfills at the 
site. Test locations and elevations were estimated by pacing and interpolating from on-site 
survey stakes. These locations and elevations should be considered accurate only to the 
degree implied by the methods used. Areas assessed to be unsatisfactory were reworked 
until the specified minimum compaction was obtained. 
Based on the observations of our field representatives and the results of the 
referenced tests, it is our opinion that the earthwork operations during the site grading, 
pavement and utility line construction for the above project observed and tested by 
Geolabs in the period covered by this report were performed in general accordance with 
the intent of the project plans and specifications, the above-referenced geotechnical 
engineering report and our subsequent recommendations. 
LIMITATIONS 
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities 
occurring simultaneously on a construction site. Therefore, some of the earthworks 
were performed without our observation. However, the level of earthwork observation 
and testing services provided appear to be reasonable in reducing some of the 
geotechnical risks to the project. It should be recognized that there are variations in the 
accuracy and statistical repeatability of the tests and methods used to monitor 
earthwork construction and materials.  
Our services were performed in accordance with generally accepted standards of 
geotechnical engineering practice; no warranty is expressed or implied. Provision of 
construction monitoring by an engineer is not insurance, nor does it guarantee 
construction of any type. The contractor shall retain responsibility for the quality of the 
work, for adhering to the plans and specifications, and for repairing defects regardless of 
when they are found.

you have questions or need additional information, please contact our office.
